## Section 001: Rust Backend Skill Entrypoint
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Skill Entrypoint", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title names one entrypoint while the two mapped skills are two different front doors, the delivery skill is the working entrypoint that turns backend requests into decision-complete work packets, and the explainer skill is a meta-entrypoint that only explains why the backend skill exists beside the broader Rust stack
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Skill Entrypoint", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because an entrypoint's job is triage before content, the delivery skill's own opening line commits it to spec-first, service-aware, production-biased packets, and its first workflow step is classification, choose the active mode set before planning or coding
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Skill Entrypoint", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: conflating the two doors sends explanation requests into work-packet machinery or backend tasks into plain-English narration, each skill's frontmatter description exists precisely to keep the triggers apart
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Skill Entrypoint", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference covers the two SKILL.md entry surfaces, the five bundle reference files behind the delivery door belong to their own corpus themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Skill Entrypoint", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to open with the two-door structure, delivery for doing backend work, explainer for justifying the skill split, and route every use through the right door first
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Skill Entrypoint", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the pair encodes a division the corpus rarely makes explicit, skills that do work versus skills that explain why work is organized a certain way, and the explainer's first guardrail, never mention the upstream source material, shows meta-skills need their own evidence discipline

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed two local rows share one usage role while carrying opposite authority shapes, the delivery skill is executable doctrine whose claims are testable against its own bundle, and the explainer is narrative positioning whose claims are about the skill stack, not about backend engineering
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because citing them interchangeably blurs claim classes, a mode definition or guardrail must cite the delivery skill, while a scope-split rationale or audience-style rule must cite the explainer, because each is authoritative only over its own genre
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: quoting the explainer for backend technique is the sharper risk, its own guardrails forbid framework detail and upstream mentions, so any technical claim attributed to it is by construction fabricated
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: provenance for this document's statements only, the four external URLs stayed unretrieved throughout this evolution and confer no current-fact authority
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to keep both rows and annotate the genre split, doctrine claims to the delivery row, positioning claims to the explainer row, chained bundle content cited by name
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the two skills even sit in different archive families, claude-skills versus codex-skills of the same 202604 month, so this theme is the corpus's clearest evidence that parallel agent ecosystems documented the same backend stack simultaneously

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide

- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each tension has a stance in the sources, the delivery skill spends ceremony to make packets decision-complete, the explainer spends precision to keep explanations accessible, and the pair exists because one skill covering both bought breadth at accuracy's expense

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: taking the seed's roles literally would route doctrine disputes to a file whose guardrails forbid it from holding doctrine, an authority loop the genre split dissolves immediately

### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **revision_decision:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: route by the funnel, admitted work down through the routing theme, stack questions to the explainer door, out-of-scope work sideways to the named broader skills
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: for platform questions no local skill covers, agent-format documentation externally labeled unretrieved This changes how the section resolves where to send a request the two entry doors should not answer.

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed endpoint-count budgets fit destination work, not entry work, whose real units are per-request dispatch performed constantly at seconds of cost, per-packet ceremony performed per work item at minutes to hours, and per-revision card upkeep performed rarely when either SKILL.md changes
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the three units scale on different axes, dispatch scales with request volume, ceremony scales with work item count and size, and upkeep scales with bundle revision frequency, so one capacity number cannot budget the entry layer
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: budgeting ceremony as dispatch, treating the full six-step workflow as a per-request reflex, either starves real packets of their requirement work or inflates trivial questions into work packets, both misallocations of the same flat model
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: budgeting entry-layer effort, implementation-slice budgets belong to the playbook theme and operational budgets to the ops theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to restate the model in three units, dispatch cost per request, ceremony cost per packet scaled by mode count, and upkeep cost per bundle revision
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that mode count is the natural ceremony multiplier, a Spec-plus-Delivery task and a Review-plus-three-risk-modes task differ predictably in packet effort, so the mode declaration made at dispatch doubles as the packet's effort estimate, one artifact serving two purposes
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to keep dispatch under a minute via the card, budget packets by their declared mode count, and slot card upkeep into every bundle revision
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the three units scale on different axes, dispatch scales with request volume, ceremony scales with work item count and size, and upkeep scales with bundle revision frequency, so one capacity number cannot budget the entry layer
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; budgeting ceremony as dispatch, treating the full six-step workflow as a per-request reflex, either starves real packets of their requirement work or inflates trivial questions into work packets, both misallocations of the same flat model
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: budgeting entry-layer effort, implementation-slice budgets belong to the playbook theme and operational budgets to the ops theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: restate the model in three units, dispatch cost per request, ceremony cost per packet scaled by mode count, and upkeep cost per bundle revision
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies mode count is the natural ceremony multiplier, a Spec-plus-Delivery task and a Review-plus-three-risk-modes task differ predictably in packet effort, so the mode declaration made at dispatch doubles as the packet's effort estimate, one artifact serving two purposes
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: request volume is high enough that dispatch efficiency matters, low-volume teams can afford slower per-request classification
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because the three units scale on different axes, dispatch scales with request volume, ceremony scales with work item count and size, and upkeep scales with bundle revision frequency, so one capacity number cannot budget the entry layer
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where budgeting ceremony as dispatch, treating the full six-step workflow as a per-request reflex, either starves real packets of their requirement work or inflates trivial questions into work packets, both misallocations of the same flat model
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by budgeting entry-layer effort, implementation-slice budgets belong to the playbook theme and operational budgets to the ops theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in request volume is high enough that dispatch efficiency matters, low-volume teams can afford slower per-request classification
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: show the second-order benefit that mode count is the natural ceremony multiplier, a Spec-plus-Delivery task and a Review-plus-three-risk-modes task differ predictably in packet effort, so the mode declaration made at dispatch doubles as the packet's effort estimate, one artifact serving two purposes
### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: budgeting ceremony as dispatch, treating the full six-step workflow as a per-request reflex, either starves real packets of their requirement work or inflates trivial questions into work packets, both misallocations of the same flat model
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are the upkeep unit is rare enough to be forgotten entirely, and a stale dispatch card silently degrades every subsequent dispatch, so upkeep belongs to the revision event itself, not to a calendar
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where request volume is high enough that dispatch efficiency matters, low-volume teams can afford slower per-request classification
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 04 on failure boundary: distinguish a genuine failure from an out-of-scope case using budgeting entry-layer effort, implementation-slice budgets belong to the playbook theme and operational budgets to the ops theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: letting agents absorb dispatch cost entirely via description matching, near-zero marginal cost, human reviewers still need the card for conformance checks

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed document-property thresholds stand where entry-layer invariants should, every response traceable to a declared door and mode set, every packet carrying all seven contract sections in order, every requirement thresholded and evidenced, and zero out-of-scope tasks answered instead of forwarded
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each target is a source rule stated as an invariant, the declaration target from the workflow's classification step, the contract target from the output contract, the threshold target from the vague-claim rejection rule, and the scope target from the first delivery guardrail
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: averaging the targets hides the ones that are binary per event, one out-of-scope task answered authoritatively is one wrong-skill artifact in circulation, not a tolerable percentage point
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: entry-layer invariants, destination-content reliability belongs to the destination themes' targets
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to publish the four targets with their evidence methods, response headers for declarations, section audits for contracts, gate records for thresholds, and dispatch logs for scope
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that all four targets are checkable from artifacts the discipline already produces, declarations, packets, gates, and logs, so enforcement adds no new instrumentation, only the habit of actually reading what the process emits

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed corpus-process bullets stand where entry-layer retry doctrine should, a failed dispatch and a failed packet retry differently, misdispatch is cheap to redo, re-classify and re-enter through the right door, while a packet failing its gates must not simply regenerate, its failure names which workflow step was starved
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because dispatch is stateless and packets are cumulative, a wrong door leaves no artifact worth salvaging, but a gate failure points backward into the packet, unmeasured claims trace to the requirements step and coverage holes to the verification mix, so the retry re-enters the workflow at the failed step, not at the start
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: regenerating a failed packet from scratch discards the diagnostic the gate failure encoded and usually reproduces the same starved step, the entry-layer version of rerunning a failed migration blindly
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: retry semantics for entry-layer work, request-level retry doctrine belongs to the security sibling's territory one layer down
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the two-regime rule, free re-dispatch for door and mode errors, and step-targeted re-entry for gate failures, with the failed gate naming the re-entry point
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the ordered workflow makes gate failures self-locating, because each gate checks one step's output, the failure message is also the retry address, a property the workflow's sequential design buys and unordered checklists lack
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to re-dispatch freely on classification errors with the card open, and re-enter at the named step on gate failures, escalating to a human after the second same-step failure
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because dispatch is stateless and packets are cumulative, a wrong door leaves no artifact worth salvaging, but a gate failure points backward into the packet, unmeasured claims trace to the requirements step and coverage holes to the verification mix, so the retry re-enters the workflow at the failed step, not at the start

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: retry semantics for entry-layer work, request-level retry doctrine belongs to the security sibling's territory one layer down
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add the two-regime rule, free re-dispatch for door and mode errors, and step-targeted re-entry for gate failures, with the failed gate naming the re-entry point

- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 08 on verification method: add pass/fail observations tied to the revision add the two-regime rule, free re-dispatch for door and mode errors, and step-targeted re-entry for gate failures, with the failed gate naming the re-entry point
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 08 on verification method: verification should also test the consequence that the ordered workflow makes gate failures self-locating, because each gate checks one step's output, the failure message is also the retry address, a property the workflow's sequential design buys and unordered checklists lack
### Question 09: What is known confidently, and what remains judgment or uncertainty?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: the confident evidence is the sequential gate-to-step coupling read from the delivery skill's workflow in full
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: the retained seed basis is all five seed retry and backpressure bullets remain preserved
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: the unresolved judgment is the same-step failure count that should trigger escalation is team-calibrated
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: confidence applies only while retry semantics for entry-layer work, request-level retry doctrine belongs to the security sibling's territory one layer down
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: label direct evidence, inference, and provisional guidance separately while implementing add the two-regime rule, free re-dispatch for door and mode errors, and step-targeted re-entry for gate failures, with the failed gate naming the re-entry point
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: preserve uncertainty because it affects the deduction that the ordered workflow makes gate failures self-locating, because each gate checks one step's output, the failure message is also the retry address, a property the workflow's sequential design buys and unordered checklists lack
### Question 10: What deeper deductions, second-order consequences, or additional insights follow, and how should they change the guidance?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the deeper deduction is that the ordered workflow makes gate failures self-locating, because each gate checks one step's output, the failure message is also the retry address, a property the workflow's sequential design buys and unordered checklists lack
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: that deduction follows from dispatch is stateless and packets are cumulative, a wrong door leaves no artifact worth salvaging, but a gate failure points backward into the packet, unmeasured claims trace to the requirements step and coverage holes to the verification mix, so the retry re-enters the workflow at the failed step, not at the start
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where regenerating a failed packet from scratch discards the diagnostic the gate failure encoded and usually reproduces the same starved step, the entry-layer version of rerunning a failed migration blindly
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: carry the deduction forward only within retry semantics for entry-layer work, request-level retry doctrine belongs to the security sibling's territory one layer down
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: add the two-regime rule, free re-dispatch for door and mode errors, and step-targeted re-entry for gate failures, with the failed gate naming the re-entry point
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: fully regenerating packets on any failure, simpler to script for agent workflows, it trades the diagnostic for idempotence and fits only fully automated pipelines This changes how the section resolves which entry-layer failures may retry immediately and which must re-enter at a named step.

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed request-latency ceilings measure the destination layer, this theme's performance surfaces are dispatch latency from request arrival to door-and-mode declaration, packet lead time from declaration to gate pass, and explanation turnaround for the plain-English door
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the entry layer's cost is process cost, its ceremony competes with delivery speed, so proving the ceremony affordable means measuring the ceremony itself, not the services it eventually produces
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: leaving entry cost unmeasured lets it be argued anecdotally in both directions, ceremony defenders cite quality and critics cite delay, and without lead-time data the argument resolves by seniority instead of evidence
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: verifying entry-layer performance, service latency methods belong to the playbook theme's SLO clause and pipeline duration to the ops theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to measure the three surfaces with trend alarms, dispatch latency per request, packet lead time split by mode count, and explanation turnaround per explainer response
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that splitting packet lead time by declared mode count is what makes the number actionable, a rising two-mode lead time signals process friction while a rising five-mode share signals harder work arriving, the same total hiding two opposite stories
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to record the three measurements from existing artifact timestamps and investigate any trend breaking its historical band
